Feature Match: Round 6 – Tim Aten vs Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Brazilian superstar Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa managed to put an exclamation point onto his Pro Tour career earlier this year by becoming crowned the champion of Pro Tour-San Juan. The event marked a milestone in PVDDR's time on Tour as he finally took home a crown after averaging a Pro Tour Top 8 per season he has played professionally. Those numbers were incredible in light of the industry average, but one player who wasn't impressed was the curmudgeonly Tim Aten. The writer, begrudgingly loved by many for his prose, was a stalwart Pro Tour competitor though of late he had been far more likely to watch a Grand Prix than compete in one. That didn't take away the fact he had multiple Top 8s to his name, including at the Pro Tour level.


**Game 1**


The first game began with Paulo on the play, but things weren't exactly exciting early. Both had utility two-drops, Aten in the form of [Sylvan Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Ranger+)  and his opponent in the form of [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton). The 1/1 was a lynchpin for comboing with [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) and [Bloodthrone Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodthrone+Vampire), but also made a nigh unkillable blocker. Tim tried to get on the board with a [Garruk's Companion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk%27s+Companion) but found it bounced by his opponent's Æther Adept. A [Nightwing Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nightwing+Shade) from Paulo was killed with [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) out of Tim.


The re-cast Companion was taken out for good by a block from the Adept, and post-combat a [Cudgel Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cudgel+Troll) hit for Aten. The 4/3 could dominate the ground but Tim was tapped out and had no green mana with which to regenerate his creature. That gave Damo da Rosa just the shot he needed to use [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) to kill it; Aten reloaded with a [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball). [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) for Paulo Vitor left him convinced it was safe to attack, and he sent his Skeleton to the red zone.


An [Awakener Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Awakener+Druid) for Aten put him in charge, awakening a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) and allowing him to crack back for 5 along with his [Sylvan Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Ranger). [Azure Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azure+Drake) hit for Paulo who was trying to come up with an edge on the battlefield before he lost to his opponent's [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball). An [Earth Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Earth+Servant) from Aten made that look increasingly less likely, but [Quag Sickness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quag+Sickness) from his Brazilian opponent took out [Awakener Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Awakener+Druid) and turned off the activated [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest), then a Skeleton block on [Sylvan Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Ranger) and a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) for [Earth Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Earth+Servant) cleared Tim's board of creatures entirely.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM6-PauloVitor.jpg)[Giant Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Spider) allowed the American, Aten, to begin rebuilding all the while peering into his [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball) for clues as to what was coming up in his draw step. [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) allowed him to take out a [Stone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stone+Golem) from his opponent, but he was still unable to attack, instead forced to stare down his opponent's 2/4 [Azure Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azure+Drake) with his own 2/4 [Giant Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Spider). Paulo Vitor threw a haymaker in the form of [Sword of Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Vengeance), but using a series of [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt)s Tim was able to keep the equipment contained by clearing his opponent's board of creatures.


A [Spined Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spined+Wurm) for Aten was quickly stolen by [Mind Control](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Control) from Damo da Rosa, then soon found itself wielding a [Sword of Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Vengeance). Tim didn't seem pleased by that and used a [Chandra's Outrage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Outrage) to kill his own creature. Still, he was slowly pecking away at Paulo's life total with the [Giant Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Spider), and still had the [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball) filtering his draws. A [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut) off the top for his opponent quickly shifted things, picking up the Sword and punching Tim to just 2 life.


That gave Aten exactly one turn to find yet another removal spell, and he activated his [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball) in an effort to do so. Sensing the game was near its end, Paulo Vitor perused his opponent's graveyard making a mental note of what was there while Tim figured out what to do with the cards on top of his library. When Aten put them on the bottom then drew a blank he promptly conceded and headed to the second game behind.


Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa 1, Tim Aten 0


"He's not thinking about mulliganing, he's plotting out his first five turns," Tim Aten said as Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa opened on seven cards and considered them deeply before declaring whether he'd keep.


"He did that to spite me!" Aten cried as Paulo did mulligan before keeping six.


**Game 2**


Trying to accelerate his opening draw, Aten cast a [Llanowar Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Llanowar+Elves) to start the second game. His opponent was ready, however, using [Quag Sickness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quag+Sickness) to take the 1/1 out before casting [Azure Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azure+Drake), [Stone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stone+Golem), and then an Æther Adept, all allowing the Brazilian to come out to a faster start. [Giant Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Spider) and [Sylvan Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Ranger) hit for Aten, but when he attempted an [Earth Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Earth+Servant) it was killed by [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak).


Paulo's bomby equipment, [Sword of Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Vengeance), agreeably hopped from the top of his library to the table and allowed him to begin putting a serious hurt on his opponent after being equipped to Æther Adept. When Tim replied with a Mitotic Ooze, Paulo Vitor switched the equipment to his [Azure Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azure+Drake) and continued attacking. [Chandra's Outrage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Outrage) answered the Drake, and a [Greater Basilisk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Greater+Basilisk) from Tim left him feeling confident enough to begin attacking with his Ooze.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM6-TimAten.JPG)Soon, however, he had a Sword-wielding [Stone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stone+Golem) to deal with. That merited a chump-block from the Basilisk, but a [Brittle Effigy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brittle+Effigy) from the American gave him a hope of containing the Sword for at least one more attack. The artifact was quickly used to deal with an [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant), but Paulo Vitor simply reloaded with a [Nightwing Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nightwing+Shade).


At 3 life, Tim Aten was spinning his wheels trying to stay alive in the match. He cast a [Fire Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fire+Servant), but needed blocks to survive against his opponent's [Sword of Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Vengeance). However, a bit of mana flood gave Aten an out: if he had a [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball) either in his hand or his deck, the [Fire Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fire+Servant) would make the card lethal by allowing it to deal 14, doubling up on the seven lands Aten could pump into the X portion of the spell's casting cost. That was exactly Paulo's life total, but the Brazilian was able to keep the pressure on, dropping his opponent to just 1 with an attack with his flyer. Did Tim have the [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball)? The world would never know as he scooped up his cards after drawing a non-[Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball) spell. . .


Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa 2, Tim Aten 0


  


Saturday, 10:53 p.m. – A Bounty on His Head
-------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Grand Prix events are famous for offering tons of things to do for **Magic** players and fans of all stripes. Here in Portland, for example, none other than Richard Garfield (the inventor of **Magic**) was here signing for fans as were a dozen artists, a half dozen dealers, a full stable of the game's biggest pros, a healthy contingent of judges, and even a well-staffed public events table. But for the just-shy-of-a-dozen players who found themselves paired against one Scott Elliott, a special extra was tossed their way. So who exactly is Scott Elliott?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/Blog%20-%20ScottElliot.JPG)The Seattle resident is the Senior Director of Sales for Gen Con, the largest gaming convention in the world. He's also an avid **Magic** player, which he has been enjoying since 1994, and decided to combine his job with his love of **Magic**. How? By putting a bounty on his own head, offering to give away badges for entry into Gen Con 2011 to all players who managed to beat him!


"I like playing **Magic** and wanted to play this event," Scott said, explaining why he had decided to run the special promotion for Gen Con. "I wanted to give something away to people who beat me, and anything that adds one additional iota of fun is worth doing." Unfortunately for players, Scott's Sealed pool was a hot one and at the time we chatted he was an impressive 4-2-1. But Scott is a generous fellow.


"I gave away a pass earlier to a woman who was a fan of ours on Facebook and Twitter, and recognized me here," Scott said, bending the rules of the bounty hunt to make sure he distributed as many of the free Gen Con badges as he could. "And I gave one to the player I drew with for being such a good sport," he added.


So what does a badge for Gen Con 2011 get you, exactly? Entrance to the event, held annually in Indianapolis, Indiana, and this past year was home to 8,000+ events over the course of the weekend, many of which were **Magic** tournaments. "We had a record breaking crowd this year," Scott said, "over 30,000 people. Gen Con 2011 is going to get bigger and better." The badges Scott was handing out over the weekend guarantee free admittance to anyone who has one.


With only a few rounds left to play, Scott clearly wasn't willing to leave with so many badges still under his care. He had spoken with tournament organizer Tim Shields about means by which he could give away additional passes, including rewarding a lucky judge for his or her hard work on the weekend. As a level 3 judge and a contributor to **Magic** organized play efforts, Scott certainly knows a thing or two about the significant effort both judges and tournament organizers go through to bring players and fans fantastic events like Grand Prix-Portland.


And if you haven't had a chance to play against Scott yet this weekend? There may still be opportunities on Sunday!


  


Feature Match: Round 7 – Arthur Halavais vs Luis Scott-Vargas
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by Josh Bennett*

In six words, Luis Scott-Vargas is a giggling punster and a master mage. Who else could Top 16 a Pro Tour and post a picture of himself pouting in a gigantic clog? This round he faced off against blogger and grinder Arthur Halavais.


The first game was quick and brutal. Halavais mulliganed, and after they traded Children of Night, LSV was happy to make things worse him with [Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter). Halavais had gotten out a sluggish [Gargoyle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gargoyle+Sentinel), but was stuck on three lands. LSV [Cultivate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cultivate)d into [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime). Some rapid beats later they were shuffling up for Game 2.


Scott-Vargas 1 - Halavais 0


Halavais put LSV on the play for the second game, and it looked like it might backfire when LSV led with [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) and [Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter) (catching an island). Halavais played his second land and took two in the air, and LSV [Cultivate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cultivate)d. Halavais set him back with [Pyroclasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyroclasm).


[Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) brought the Specter back for another round. Halavais made no play. LSV hit for two and played [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night). Still no move from Halavais. LSV hit him again and decided to play the Specter, catching a mountain. Halavais cleared out the 2/1s with a [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball).


LSV gamely hit for two more, but with six land in play and three cards in hand he passed the turn. Halavais played his land and passed. Another two from LSV. At end of turn, Halavais cast [Jace's Ingenuity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%27s+Ingenuity). He untapped and cast [Mind Rot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Rot), stealing swamp and [Quag Sickness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quag+Sickness). LSV played a land and hit him to eight.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM7-Halavais.JPG)Halavais untapped and played a second [Mind Rot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Rot) for LSV's last card: [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball). [Scroll Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Thief) put a stop to the [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) beats. LSV drew and passed. Now Halavais was moving fast. He played [Gargoyle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gargoyle+Sentinel). LSV played [Nature's Spiral](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Spiral) for [Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter) and cast it immediately, with three up. Halavais discarded [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak). He had no play on his turn.


LSV swung in with his Specter and Halavais turned on his Sentinel. LSV was ready with [Plummet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plummet). Halavais fell to six. He played out the last of his hand, a [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night) and an Æther Adept for the Specter. LSV replayed it, along with a [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night) of his own.


Halavais drew and played [Foresee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Foresee). LSV's face fell a little. He brought out [Whispersilk Cloak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Whispersilk+Cloak) and gave it to his Thief, attacking for a card. LSV had a Cloak of his own, suiting up his Child and bringing Halavais down to just two life.


Halavais wasn't done yet. Down came [Sword of Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Vengeance). His Child picked it up and he swung in with Thief and Child, back up to six. He added a [Black Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Knight) to the table. LSV's attack brought him back down to two, and his deck served up another winner: [Garruk's Packleader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk%27s+Packleader). Now, between Specter and Packleader, he could swing for six.


Unfortunately for him, Halavais was rolling. He swung in for more life. The totals were sixteen to six against. Down came [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant). Again LSV was locked out of swinging for the win. He put Halavais back to two with the cloaked Packleader and [Cultivate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cultivate)d some swamps.


[Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant) and [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night) hit for eight. LSV put Halavais back to two but his back was against the wall. Halavais activated his Sentinel and attacked with it, the Servant and the Child. LSV tapped two... [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade)! Down went the [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant), leaving LSV at one life, suddenly free to swing with his Specter on his turn. The win was within his grasp.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM7-LSV.JPG)And then Halavais played [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger), replaying his [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant).


LSV plucked his top card and hid it, very slowly peeking at it. After the corner came into view, he scooped up his cards for Game 3.


Scott-Vargas 1 - Halavais 1


LSV got to be on the draw for the deciding game, and met Halavais's [Steel Overseer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Overseer) with [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night). A [Mind Rot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Rot) from Halavais gave LSV pause. He eventually pitched [Whispersilk Cloak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Whispersilk+Cloak) and [Nature's Spiral](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Spiral). He untapped, hit for two, then passed the turn, stuck on a pair of swamps.


Halavais sent the Child back with Æther Adept. LSV found a forest and [Cultivate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cultivate)d for swamps. Halavais added a [Rotting Legion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rotting+Legion) to his team. LSV stopped the Overseer with [Quag Sickness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quag+Sickness), and replayed his Child. Halavais swung in and LSV traded for the Adept. Next up from Halavais was [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant).


LSV summoned a [Spined Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spined+Wurm) and hoped for the best. The best was not forthcoming. Instead, it was a [Sword of Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Vengeance) for the [Rotting Legion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rotting+Legion) and an attack for ten. LSV drew his next card and shook his head, then conceded.


Arthur Halavais defeats Luis Scott-Vargas 2-1


  


Saturday, 11:35 p.m. – Build Along With Coverage - Brian Kibler
---------------------------------------------------------------


*by Josh Bennett*

I stole a few minutes of Brian Kibler's time way back in round three while he enjoyed his third bye. Now that you've seen the amateurs handle this pool, it's time for a pro to tackle it.


He spread the pool out quickly, shelving red immediately and reducing the green to a handful of cards. For the other three colors he split off the creatures by casting cost and looked at how they measured up.


He started blue-white, moving cards in and out quickly and frowning. Then he stripped off all the blue and tried marrying it to the black.


"I think probably blue-white. This deck just doesn't have enough cards. I mean, Liliana's Spectre is great. Maybe if it had a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) and something else. As is, it just doesn't do anything."


He piled up the blue-white again.


"I'm not sure about this [Honor of the Pure](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Honor+of+the+Pure). I think it's close. You probably want it. It won't always work, but it makes your best draws awesome."


[Palace Guard](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Palace+Guard) came in as a late addition, booting an [Augury Owl](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augury+Owl). The last spells to be cut were [Inspired Charge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inspired+Charge) and [Whispersilk Cloak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Whispersilk+Cloak).


"Charge is pretty good in a deck like this, but I'd cut it. [Whispersilk Cloak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Whispersilk+Cloak) is just too bad, your guys are so small. You already have better ways to push them through. You'll bring in the [Diminish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diminish) against green, but your guys are too small to use it effectively otherwise."


Asked about the format generally, he had this to say:


"I think the most common color is blue, that's why you always want [Harbor Serpent](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Serpent). You don't want [Celestial Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Purge) because most black and red creatures are terrible. I'll always maindeck [Deathmark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathmark), since green is excellent and they always have something to kill, but a card like [Flashfreeze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flashfreeze), you have to hold mana up, which is too much of a cost."







#### Kibler's Build

Sunday, 12:35 a.m. – Photo Essay
--------------------------------


*by Josh Bennett*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/chuckLucacks.jpg)There is an actual Artists' Alley here this weekend. Chuck Lucacks shows off his work.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/coreyMacourek.jpg)And that's Corey Macourek!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/franzVohwinkel.jpg)Franz Vohwinkel poses while Tuk-Tuk the Returned looks on.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/heatherHudson.jpg)Holy Moses it's Heather Hudson! She did Basking Rootwalla, Wall of Blossoms, Hermit Druid, and a hundred and eighty other cards, not all of them green and brutal.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/jaimejones.jpg)Jaime Jones, the man behind the incredible Progenitus.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/KekaiKotaki.jpg)Kekai Kotaki brought Lorthos, the Tidemaker to life.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/mikedringenberg.jpg)Mike Dringenberg helped haunt Shadowmoor with Painter's Servant.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/MarkTedin.jpg)Mark Tedin's been bringing the game to life since Alpha, and is not slowing down.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/rkpost.jpg)You might think that rk post can't reach into your head and harvest your nightmares, but you'd be wrong.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/peteventers.jpg)Pete Venters. TWO HUNDRED AND SEVENTY FOUR CARDS.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/robalexander.jpg)Rob Alexander's another veteran. The man behind some of the most forbidding locales in the game.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/ansonmaddocks.jpg)Seriously. That's Anson Maddocks. The actual Anson Maddocks, not one of the many Anson Maddocks impersonators.


I can't stress this enough: If you love Magic art, and you can come down to Portland, you're going to regret it if you don't come on Sunday.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/chuckLucaksLandTax.jpg)I think that's a Land Tax, but where's the moustache?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/alteredcards.jpg)More sweet "artist-enhanced" cards.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/garfieldSigning.jpg)The Father of Magic, his bowtie rakishly askew.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/GarfieldShirt.jpg)Look at the joy on that face.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/ochoawaitsinchair.jpg)While the rest of the world stands in line, David Ochoa asserts his mastery by bringing a chair.


  


Feature Match: Round 8 – Yuuya Watanabe vs Shuhei Nakamura
----------------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

As Grand Prix-Portland wound its way down to the end of the first day of competition, the feature match for the eighth round found reigning Player of the Year Yuuya Watanabe squaring off against fellow Japanese countryman and former Player of the Year Shuhei Nakamura. The two players had traveled halfway across the world, only to find themselves battling against each other late in the day.


**Game 1**


Yuuya won the die roll but it was Shuhei who came out of the gates fastest. His opening turns were a flurry of spells, beginning with [Infantry Veteran](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infantry+Veteran) and including [Stormfront Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormfront+Pegasus), [Blinding Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blinding+Mage), and [Brittle Effigy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brittle+Effigy). Across the table Watanabe had managed a lone [Cloud Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloud+Elemental), but as the PoY reached four mana he considered a number of options in his hand. Tapping out Watanabe plopped a [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut) to the battlefield before passing the turn.


The [Stormfront Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormfront+Pegasus) headed to the red zone for Shuhei, trading for the [Cloud Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloud+Elemental) after a timely assist from Nakamura's [Infantry Veteran](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infantry+Veteran). Yuuya fired back with an attack via his [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut) before casting a post-combat [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant). Looking for some help from his library, Shuhei sacrificed his [Infantry Veteran](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infantry+Veteran) to scry with [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer). The play found him an [Assassinate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassinate), which he was able to use on his opponent's [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM8-Nakamura.JPG)[Combust](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Combust) from Yuuya took out [Blinding Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blinding+Mage) from Nakamura and allowed the [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut) free reign on the battlefield. A [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball) for Yuuya threatened to allow him to run away with things, and his opponent was forced to use [Brittle Effigy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brittle+Effigy) in an attempt to kill the [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut). A timely [Unsummon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unsummon) from Watanabe saved the creature, and the two were back where they had started as the 5/3 returned to the battlefield.


[Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan) for Shuhei pulled him right back into things, returning [Blinding Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blinding+Mage) to the battlefield and forcing Yuuya to dig for help with his [Crystal Ball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Ball). [Ice Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ice+Cage) helped the pro contain the 6/6 mythic from Nakamura, and the [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut) continued to attack. [Roc Egg](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Roc+Egg) for Shuhei hoped to chump for a turn, but when his opponent revealed a [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball) in his hand for the final points of damage straight to Shuhei's head, the former Player of the Year conceded to the reigning one.


Yuuya Watanabe 1, Shuhei Nakamura 0


**Game 2**


Shuhei Nakamura attempted to start aggressively in the second game as he had in the first. The problem? His second-turn [Stormfront Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormfront+Pegasus) was immediately stopped by an [Ice Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ice+Cage) from his opponent. The enchantment didn't last long, however, as a [Blinding Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blinding+Mage) from Shuhei allowed him to target his own creature, shattering the Cage made of Ice.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM8-Watanabe.JPG)The battlefield soon was a mirror image for the two players, each having a [Wild Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wild+Griffin) and a [Stormfront Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormfront+Pegasus). The foursome of creatures traded in combat, and Shuhei followed up with [Chandra's Spitfire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Spitfire). Soon after, however, Yuuya burst onto the table with a [Serra Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Angel) followed by [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan). The duo of creatures was a powerful force to be reckoned with, and Shuhei was going to find himself in deep trouble if he was unable to come up with a solution quickly.


His own Titan was a start, as his copy of [Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan) hit the battlefield and returned a [Wild Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wild+Griffin) from the graveyard. Yuuya pressed on, casting [Siege Mastodon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Siege+Mastodon) and using an Æther Adept to bounce his opponent's [Chandra's Spitfire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Spitfire). He was then able to use [Unsummon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unsummon) when the 1/3 was re-cast and had exactly enough damage to attack for lethal thanks to his Titan and [Serra Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Angel). Despite drawing his mythic, Shuhei was done in out of seemingly nowhere.


Yuuya Watanabe 2, Shuhei Nakamura 0


  


Feature Match: Round 9 – Andrew Veen vs Gerry Thompson
------------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Andrew Veen and Gerry Thompson sat down in good position at Grand Prix-Portland for the final match of the day. Veen, who hailed from the Pacific Northwest, originally came from the Midwest where Gerry was also from. The two knew each other well from days spent PTQing, but with Top 8 hopes up for risk they were good natured but down to business.


**Game 1**


[Black Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Knight) led the charge for Andrew Veen, but the 2/2 was quickly matched by [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin) from Thompson. [Ice Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ice+Cage) turned the Assassin off, but Thompson just fired back with [Gargoyle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gargoyle+Sentinel). The 3/3 artifact creature was bounced back to his hand as Andrew cast Æther Adept to return it, but Gerry just reloaded by re-casting his card and adding a [Stormfront Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormfront+Pegasus) for good measure.


With the 3/3 back on the battlefield Andrew didn't have a profitable block and was forced to stay home, increasing his team by a [Scroll Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Thief). His opponent got busy with a planeswalker, [Liliana Vess](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+Vess), forcing Andrew to discard a card. That prompted a return-fire attack which saw Veen send his entire team at the opposing planeswalker, including a [Bloodthrone Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodthrone+Vampire). Gerry placed his [Gargoyle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gargoyle+Sentinel) in front of the Bloodthrone and his Pegasus in front of Æther Adept. Veen thought long and hard before sacrificing all of his creatures save the blocked Adept to keep his Bloodthrone alive.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM9-AndrewVeen.JPG)Thompson, pleased with his trade of two creatures for his opponent's three, untapped and incremented Liliana before casting a [Howling Banshee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Howling+Banshee). The 3/3 soon traded for Veen's team as he topdecked a creature to feed to his Bloodthrone and crashed it into the [Banshee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Banshee). Thompson cast a [Rotting Legion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rotting+Legion), but had it bounced momentarily by [Unsummon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unsummon). With Liliana on enough loyalty to use her ultimate, Andrew Veen did not have long to live. He double checked that the planeswalker was indeed ready to blow up, and opted to concede.


Gerry Thompson 1, Andrew Veen 0


"You're three colors, I don't imagine your mana is very good," Gerry teased his opponent before the second game.


"You take that back!" Andrew mockingly shouted back.


**Game 2**


A [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) was the first spell of the second game, coming on the first turn for Andrew Veen. Both players remained void of action after that until the third turn when Gerry Thompson finally cast a spell: [Cloud Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloud+Elemental). The 2/3 was dead almost as soon as it hit the battlefield, though Veen was down a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) to kill it. [Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter) from Veen forced his opponent to discard [Assassinate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassinate), and a Gerry T [Howling Banshee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Howling+Banshee) was exiled with [Celestial Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Purge).


[Steel Overseer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Overseer) finally stuck for Gerry, though he was behind in the race to his opponent's Specter. The Overseer slowly began accumulating +1/+1 counters, but a [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast) from Veen put an even bigger clock to Gerry's head. He dug for some help by casting [Jace's Ingenuity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%27s+Ingenuity), finding [Gargoyle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gargoyle+Sentinel). With help from [Steel Overseer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Overseer), Gerry managed to take out the [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast) and had a [Cancel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cancel) when Veen attempted a [Howling Banshee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Howling+Banshee) of his own.


The [Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter) continued working its magic on Gerry's life total, and a [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin) for Thompson turned on him as Andrew stole it with [Mind Control](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Control). Still digging for solutions to the Specter, Thompson cast [Sign in Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sign+in+Blood) targeting himself. That found him [Assassinate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassinate) to take out the 2/1, but still left him facing off against his own stolen Assassin. When he tried to [Quag Sickness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quag+Sickness) the creature, however, Veen revealed a trick: [Stabbing Pain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stabbing+Pain) to target the [Steel Overseer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Overseer), Gerry's last blocker, which he could then kill by activating the Assassin. About to take lethal damage, Gerry conceded the game evening things at one a piece.


Gerry Thompson 1, Andrew Veen 1


**Game 3**


The third game spelled mulligans for both players, each sending their opening seven cards back for six. Both kept those hands and promptly got underway. Thompson led with a [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night), but his [Bog Raiders](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bog+Raiders) was felled by [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak). [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast) from Veen soon shut down attacks out of the 2/1 Child, but Gerry continued accruing creatures to his side of the battlefield by casting a [Scroll Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Thief).


Reaching across the table to ask judge Niko Skartvedt a question, Andrew Veen verified his [Clone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clone) wouldn't blow up his own [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast) if it was set to copy the 4/5. When Niko confirmed it would not, Andrew doubled up on his Phantoms before passing the turn. His opponent had only [Steel Overseer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Overseer), beginning to fall behind to the two 4/5s. The Beasts crashed in to make the score 18-10 in Veen's favor and post-combat Andrew attempted [Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter), which was countered by a second [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) from Thompson. [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) shut down the [Scroll Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Thief) and Andrew passed the turn.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppor10/FM9-GerryThompson.JPG)[Assassinate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassinate) from Gerry took out the real [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast) but his opponent just re-upped by casting [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant). Did Thompson have answers to his opponent's chubby beaters? [Gargoyle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gargoyle+Sentinel) appeared for him, preparing to take out the [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant) if given the chance, but Thompson was still behind on the battlefield. With the turn back, Andrew thought for a second before sending his team sideways. Gerry took out the [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast) with a block from both his Gargoyle and [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night), gaining 2 but falling to 6 overall.


[Liliana's Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Specter) gave Gerry a blocker momentarily for the [Air Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Air+Servant), but Veen used his mana to tap the 2/1 with the 4/3's ability before untapping, attacking Gerry to 4, and casting [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast). Thompson had a single draw step to come up with an out.


He drew, then began counting damage out loud. An Æther Adept allowed him to blow up the [Phantom Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantom+Beast), and he attacked to put Veen to 4 while upping his own life to 6 with [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night). Now it was Gerry's turn to go on the offensive, and Veen had only a single draw step to come up with a solution. He drew and passed, but when Thompson correctly attacked with his entire team, Andrew was dead.


Gerry Thompson defeats Andrew Veen 2-1.
